                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Further conventions for NMR shielding and chemical shifts: (IUPAC recommendations 2008)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Harris, Robin K.; Becker, Edwin D.; Cabral De Menezes, Sonia M.; Granger, Pierre; Hoffman, Roy E.; Zilm, Kurt W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Pure and Applied Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">80</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">59-84</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PACHAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0033-4545</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">International Union of Pure and Applied Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  IUPAC has published a no. of recommendations regarding the reporting of NMR data, esp. chem. shifts.  The most recent publication recommended that tetramethylsilane (TMS) serve as a universal ref. for reporting the shifts of all nuclides, but it deferred recommendations for several aspects of this subject.  This document 1st examines the extent to which the 1H shielding in TMS itself is subject to change by variation in temp., concn., and solvent.  From recently published results, the shielding of TMS in soln. [along with that of sodium-3-(trimethylsilyl)propanesulfonate, DSS, often used as a ref. for aq. solns.] varies only slightly with temp. but is subject to solvent perturbations of a few tenths of a part per million (ppm).  Recommendations are given for reporting chem. shifts under most routine exptl. conditions and for quantifying effects of temp. and solvent variation, including the use of magnetic susceptibility corrections and of magic-angle spinning (MAS).  This document provides the 1st IUPAC recommendations for referencing and reporting chem. shifts in solids, based on high-resoln. MAS studies.  Procedures are given for relating 13C NMR chem. shifts in solids to the scales used for high-resoln. studies in the liq. phase.  The notation and terminol. used for describing chem. shift and shielding tensors in solids are reviewed in some detail, and recommendations are given for best practice.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpM-i0oONIjZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liq20QDFd9cXg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXns1Ggsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=5136168c5843eba2fc44c2e60b4c99b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Coelho, A.</span></span> <i>Topas 4.1</i>; <span class="NLM_publisher-name">Coelho Software</span>: <span class="NLM_publisher-loc">Brisbane, Australia</span>, <span class="NLM_year">2007</span>.</span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="http://scholar.google.com/scholar_lookup?hl=en&amp;publication_year=2007&amp;author=A.+Coelho&amp;title=Topas+4.1" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">QUANTUM ESPRESSO: a modular and open-source software project for quantum simulations of materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Giannozzi Paolo; Baroni Stefano; Bonini Nicola; Calandra Matteo; Car Roberto; Cavazzoni Carlo; Ceresoli Davide; Chiarotti Guido L; Cococcioni Matteo; Dabo Ismaila; Dal Corso Andrea; de Gironcoli Stefano; Fabris Stefano; Fratesi Guido; Gebauer Ralph; Gerstmann Uwe; Gougoussis Christos; Kokalj Anton; Lazzeri Michele; Martin-Samos Layla; Marzari Nicola; Mauri Francesco; Mazzarello Riccardo; Paolini Stefano; Pasquarello Alfredo; Paulatto Lorenzo; Sbraccia Carlo; Scandolo Sandro; Sclauzero Gabriele; Seitsonen Ari P; Smogunov Alexander; Umari Paolo; Wentzcovitch Renata M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of physics. Condensed matter : an Institute of Physics journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">39</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">395502</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">QUANTUM ESPRESSO is an integrated suite of computer codes for electronic-structure calculations and materials modeling, based on density-functional theory, plane waves, and pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft, and projector-augmented wave).  The acronym ESPRESSO stands for opEn Source Package for Research in Electronic Structure, Simulation, and Optimization.  It is freely available to researchers around the world under the terms of the GNU General Public License.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO builds upon newly-restructured electronic-structure codes that have been developed and tested by some of the original authors of novel electronic-structure algorithms and applied in the last twenty years by some of the leading materials modeling groups worldwide.  Innovation and efficiency are still its main focus, with special attention paid to massively parallel architectures, and a great effort being devoted to user friendliness.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO is evolving towards a distribution of independent and interoperable codes in the spirit of an open-source project, where researchers active in the field of electronic-structure calculations are encouraged to participate in the project by contributing their own codes or by implementing their own ideas into existing codes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcToTWfovXAMx7xanA7vODO6fW6udTcc2eZVWTSTE_EYqLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3Mjltl2lug%253D%253D&amp;md5=da053fa748721b6b381051a20e7a7f53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref61'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceresoli, D.</span></span> Pseudopotentials, <a href="https://sites.google.com/site/dceresoli/pseudopotentials" class="extLink">https://sites.google.com/site/dceresoli/pseudopotentials</a>.</span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="http://scholar.google.com/scholar?hl=en&amp;q=Ceresoli%2C+D.+Pseudopotentials%2C+https%3A%2F%2Fsites.google.com%2Fsite%2Fdceresoli%2Fpseudopotentials." target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy d. is the main property of rechargeable batteries that has driven the entire technol. forward in past decades.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) now surpass other, previously competitive battery types (for example, lead-acid and nickel metal hydride) but still require extensive further improvement to, in particular, extend the operation hours of mobile IT devices and the driving mileages of all-elec. vehicles.  In this Review, we present a crit. overview of a wide range of post-LIB materials and systems that could have a pivotal role in meeting such demands.  We divide battery systems into two categories: near-term and long-term technologies.  To provide a realistic and balanced perspective, we describe the operating principles and remaining issues of each post-LIB technol., and also evaluate these materials under com. cell configurations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmrufRRuizrLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLkYByTTL5PQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVert7k%253D&amp;md5=3d2782c5ebf801e43442f01f2206379f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1149/2.0151514jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Research on electrochem. Na intercalation in battery system has been reported since the early 1980s but Na-ion batteries are not commercialized so far though studies on Li-ion batteries have been reported since the late 1970s and the practical batteries have been extensively utilized for portable device applications in the world since 1991.  Now, targeted application of research and development for rechargeable batteries has changed toward realization of the sustainable energy society.  With the change in social situation and development of the battery technol., studies on Na-ion batteries have been attracted significant interests since 2010.  Although research interests of the electrode materials for Na-ion batteries are evoked in many researchers, advantages, disadvantages, and issues are not fully discussed for realizing the commercialization of Na-ion batteries.  In this article, practical issues and perspective are reviewed on the basis of mainly authors exptl. experiences, know-how, and results, and the future direction is proposed to overcome the issues and to challenge the advanced performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpYwzRdNDPiOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhLkYByTTL5PQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslelu7rP&amp;md5=62e60c3bebba851c240ed46742ea12a0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kundu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Talaie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duffort, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nazar, L. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5884</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c2ee02781j</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5884-5901</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liI7DQJ0ePsug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201700098"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mani, U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liI7DQJ0ePsug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA06467D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The rapid consumption of nonrenewable resources resulted in an ever-increasing problem of CO2 emissions that has motivated people for studying the harvesting of energy from renewable alternatives (e.g. solar and wind).  Efficient electrochem. energy storage devices play a crucial role in storing harvested energies in the daily lives.  For example, rechargeable batteries can store energy generated by solar cells during the daytime and release it during night-time.  In particular, Li-ion batteries (LIBs) have received considerable attention ever since their early commercialization in 1990s.  However, with initiatives by several governments to build large-scale energy grids to store energy for cities, problems such as the high cost and limited availability of Li starts to become major issues.  Na, which also belongs to Group 1 of the periodic table, has comparable electrochem. properties to Li, and more importantly it is considerably more accessible than Li.  Nonetheless, research into Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is currently still in its infancy compared to LIBs, although great leaps and bounds have been made recently in terms of research and development into this technol.  Here in this review, the authors summarize the recent advancements made, also covering the prospective materials for both the battery cathode and anode.  Addnl., opinions on possible solns. through correlating trends in recent papers will be suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqaYAOgglkaCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liI7DQJ0ePsug"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus-carbon nanocomposite anodes for lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramireddy, Thrinathreddy; Xing, Tan; Rahman, Md Mokhlesur; Chen, Ying; Dutercq, Quentin; Gunzelmann, Daniel; Glushenkov, Alexey M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5572-5584</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the expected theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, P is considered to be the highest capacity anode material for Na-ion batteries and one of the most attractive anode materials for Li-ion systems.  This work presents a comprehensive study of P-C nanocomposite anodes for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The composite electrodes are able to display high initial capacities of ∼1700 and 1300 mA h g-1 in Li and Na half-cells, resp., when the cells are tested within a larger potential windows of 2.0-0.01 V vs. Li/Li+ and Na/Na+.  The level of demonstrated capacity is underpinned by the storage mechanism, based on the transformation of P to Li3P phase for Li cells and an incomplete transformation to Na3P phase for Na cells.  The capacity deteriorates upon cycling, which is shown to originate from disintegration of electrodes and their delamination from current collectors by post-cycling ex situ electron microscopy.  Stable cyclic performance at the level of ∼700 and ∼350-400 mA h g-1 can be achieved if the potential windows are restricted to 2.0-0.67 V vs. Li/Li+ for Li and 2-0.33 vs. Na/Na+ for Na half-cells.  The results are critically discussed in light of literature reports.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbpTdmNtgwtrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liI7DQJ0ePsug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXit1aqt7o%253D&amp;md5=964498820e44c8f37b2e4e369def7076</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1021/nl502759z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gordin, M.                         rightTab-cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liBBgPxxV2fTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b07931"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nitta, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, H.-R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gordon, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gresham, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luzinov, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yushin, G.</span></span> <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1007/s11581-017-2339-8</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red phosphorus composite anodes for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Li; Zhou, Zhaohui; Li, Jiangang; He, Xiangming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">303-308</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IONIFA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0947-7047</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Thickness changes assocd. with charging and discharging challenge the practical application of electrodes composed of high-capacity materials towards batteries of both high energy d. and long life.  The investigation on the electrode level has found that the red phosphorus composite electrodes experience reversible expansion and shrinkage during lithiation/delithiation, except for the first cycle.  The reversible thickness changes are acceptable for the practical application, and the thickness change is only 4 μm, which is about 7% of the total thickness when the capacity d. of the electrode is 4.5 mAh cm-2. 4.5 mAh cm-2 is the upper limitation of the capacity d. for practical Li-ion batteries.  The capacity of the electrode material is 800 mAh g-1 with coulombic efficiency of 99.7%.  Such high capacity, high coulombic efficiency, and low electrode thickness change show promise of the red phosphorus composite as a practical anode for lithium-ion batteries.  This investigation pushes forward the practical application of red phosphorus composite anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrsKkFPnbRMurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liBBgPxxV2fTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVensb3I&amp;md5=ee6f0a21038a822746b80b4eb4e5b9a7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.04.168"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span> <i>J.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.043</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Utilizing a graphene matrix to overcome the intrinsic limitations of red phosphorus as an anode material in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yue, Zishuang; Gupta, Tushar; Wang, Fan; Li, Chao; Kumar, Rajesh; Yang, Zhenyu; Koratkar, Nikhil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">127</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">588-595</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red P (P) shows enormous potential as a high-performance and cost-effective Li-ion anode material.  It alloys with Li forming Li3P, which translates to a theor. capacity of ∼2595 mAh/g (∼7 times better than graphite).  The cost of bulk P is comparable to battery-grade graphite.  However, there are 2 intrinsic limitations that prevent deployment of P, viz., its low elec. cond. and its high vol. change on cycling that leads to pulverization and loss of elec. contact.  Here, we present an approach to concurrently address both limitations.  We used electro-spraying and far-IR redn. (FIR) to fabricate composites of P and reduced graphene oxide (rGO).  The electro-spraying process enables ultra-small P particles (5-10 nm), which suppresses stress-induced pulverization and drastically reduces Li-ion diffusion distances.  The low elec. cond. of P is also not a limitation at such small particle sizes.  FIR establishes C-P bonds that prevent surface migration and agglomeration of P, and enable efficient electron transfer between the rGO matrix and P nanoparticles.  The P/rGO anode delivers outstanding specific capacity (∼1763 mAh/g at c.d. of ∼0.1 A/g), extraordinary high-rate capability (≤40 A/g) and long cycle-life (&gt;1000 cycles with ∼99% coulombic efficiency).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJD0kT8EmEQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liBBgPxxV2fTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVKltL%252FF&amp;md5=a59da4079fe23ebf71d32380ef175fd8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1149/2.0351807jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tojo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamaguchi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Furukawa, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aoyanagi, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Umezaki, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Inada, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakurai, Y.</span></span> <i>J.                 10.1021/jacs.6b02882</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solid Electrolyte Interphase Growth and Capacity Loss in Silicon Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Michan, Alison L.; Divitini, Giorgio; Pell, Andrew J.; Leskes, Michal; Ducati, Caterina; Grey, Clare P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">138</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7918-7931</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) of the high capacity anode material Si is monitored over multiple electrochem. cycles by 7Li, 19F, and 13C solid-state NMR spectroscopies, with the orgs. dominating the SEI.  Homonuclear correlation expts. are used to identify the org. fragments -OCH2CH2O-, -OCH2CH2-, -OCH2CH3, and -CH2CH3 contained in both oligomeric species and lithium semicarbonates ROCO2Li, RCO2Li.  The SEI growth is correlated with increasing electrode tortuosity by using focused ion beam and SEM.  A two-stage model for lithiation capacity loss is developed: initially, the lithiation capacity steadily decreases, Li+ is irreversibly consumed at a steady rate, and pronounced SEI growth is seen.  Later, below 50% of the initial lithiation capacity, less Si is (de)lithiated resulting in less vol. expansion and contraction; the rate of Li+ being irreversibly consumed declines, and the Si SEI thickness stabilizes.  The decreasing lithiation capacity is primarily attributed to kinetics, the increased electrode tortuosity severely limiting Li+ ion diffusion through the bulk of the electrode.  The resulting changes in the lithiation processes seen in the electrochem. capacity curves are ascribed to non-uniform lithiation, the reaction commencing near the separator/on the surface of the particles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlHz_42qOjZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liBBgPxxV2fTA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XovVWktr4%253D&amp;md5=b5904ac99b906fa7a6054ce2093b1994</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.03.051"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mortazavi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Birbilis, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Medhekar, N.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A new method for sepg. isotropic and anisotropic chem.-shift interactions in magic-angle-spinning NMR is presented.  The new method is based upon manipulation of the phases of spinning sidebands using sequences of five π pulses.  A two-dimensional pulse scheme separates the spinning sidebands by order.  The amplitudes of the spinning sidebands may be analyzed to obtain the principal values of the chem.-shift anisotropy.  For sites with many sidebands, it is possible to improve the signal-to-noise ratio considerably by skew projection of the two-dimensional spectrum.  Exptl. demonstrations are presented.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoV5pMzWCUD2LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5uwmXMX3fBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2MXntVOmurw%253D&amp;md5=696b21caa94c97c1480cc58d8024bec7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref53" class="rightTabRefNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit53" data-doi="10.1351/pac200880010059"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Harris, R.                         rightTab-cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Further conventions for NMR shielding and chemical shifts: (IUPAC recommendations 2008)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Harris, Robin K.; Becker, Edwin D.; Cabral De Menezes, Sonia M.; Granger, Pierre; Hoffman, Roy E.; Zilm, Kurt W.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Pure and Applied Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2008</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">80</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">59-84</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PACHAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0033-4545</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">International Union of Pure and Applied Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  IUPAC has published a no. of recommendations regarding the reporting of NMR data, esp. chem. shifts.  The most recent publication recommended that tetramethylsilane (TMS) serve as a universal ref. for reporting the shifts of all nuclides, but it deferred recommendations for several aspects of this subject.  This document 1st examines the extent to which the 1H shielding in TMS itself is subject to change by variation in temp., concn., and solvent.  From recently published results, the shielding of TMS in soln. [along with that of sodium-3-(trimethylsilyl)propanesulfonate, DSS, often used as a ref. for aq. solns.] varies only slightly with temp. but is subject to solvent perturbations of a few tenths of a part per million (ppm).  Recommendations are given for reporting chem. shifts under most routine exptl. conditions and for quantifying effects of temp. and solvent variation, including the use of magnetic susceptibility corrections and of magic-angle spinning (MAS).  This document provides the 1st IUPAC recommendations for referencing and reporting chem. shifts in solids, based on high-resoln. MAS studies.  Procedures are given for relating 13C NMR chem. shifts in solids to the scales used for high-resoln. studies in the liq. phase.  The notation and terminol. used for describing chem. shift and shielding tensors in solids are reviewed in some detail, and recommendations are given for best practice.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpM-i0oONIjZ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5uwmXMX3fBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1cXns1Ggsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=5136168c5843eba2fc44c2e60b4c99b7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Coelho, A.</span></span> <i>Topas 4.1</i>; <span class="NLM_publisher-name">Coelho Software</span>: <span class="NLM_publisher-loc">Brisbane, Australia</span>, <span class="NLM_year">2007</span>.</span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                10.1524/zkri.220.5.567.65075</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First principles methods using CASTEP</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Clark, Stewart J.; Segall, Matthew D.; Pickard, Chris J.; Hasnip, Phil J.; Probert, Matt I.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The CASTEP code for first principles electronic structure calcns. is described. Rev. Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1996</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>77</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3865</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1103/PhysRevLett.77.3865</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="

        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">77</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3865-3868</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRLTAO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0031-9007</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) for the exchange-correlation energy improve upon the local spin d. (LSD) description of atoms, mols., and solids.  We present a simple derivation of a simple GGA, in which all parameters (other than those in LSD) are fundamental consts.  Only general features of the detailed construction underlying the Perdew-Wang 1991 (PW91) GGA are invoked.  Improvements over PW91 include an accurate description of the linear response of the uniform electron gas, correct behavior under uniform scaling, and a smoother potential.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokga1tVzFw07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUnsH74YZ69w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28XmsVCgsbs%253D&amp;md5=55943538406ee74f93aabdf882cd4630</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref58" class="rightTabRefNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit58" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.13.5188"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monkhorst, H.                 10.1088/0953-8984/21/39/395502</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">QUANTUM ESPRESSO: a modular and open-source software project for quantum simulations of materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Giannozzi Paolo; Baroni Stefano; Bonini Nicola; Calandra Matteo; Car Roberto; Cavazzoni Carlo; Ceresoli Davide; Chiarotti Guido L; Cococcioni Matteo; Dabo Ismaila; Dal Corso Andrea; de Gironcoli Stefano; Fabris Stefano; Fratesi Guido; Gebauer Ralph; Gerstmann Uwe; Gougoussis Christos; Kokalj Anton; Lazzeri Michele; Martin-Samos Layla; Marzari Nicola; Mauri Francesco; Mazzarello Riccardo; Paolini Stefano; Pasquarello Alfredo; Paulatto Lorenzo; Sbraccia Carlo; Scandolo Sandro; Sclauzero Gabriele; Seitsonen Ari P; Smogunov Alexander; Umari Paolo; Wentzcovitch Renata M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of physics. Condensed matter : an Institute of Physics journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">39</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">395502</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">QUANTUM ESPRESSO is an integrated suite of computer codes for electronic-structure calculations and materials modeling, based on density-functional theory, plane waves, and pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft, and projector-augmented wave).  The acronym ESPRESSO stands for opEn Source Package for Research in Electronic Structure, Simulation, and Optimization.  It is freely available to researchers around the world under the terms of the GNU General Public License.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO builds upon newly-restructured electronic-structure codes that have been developed and tested by some of the original authors of novel electronic-structure algorithms and applied in the last twenty years by some of the leading materials modeling groups worldwide.  Innovation and efficiency are still its main focus, with special attention paid to massively parallel architectures, and a great effort being devoted to user friendliness.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO is evolving towards a distribution of independent and interoperable codes in the spirit of an open-source project, where researchers active in the field of electronic-structure calculations are encouraged to participate in the project by contributing their own codes or by implementing their own ideas into existing codes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcToTWfovXAMx7xanA7vODO6fW6udTcc2eZENZUsV165Qrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3Mjltl2lug%253D%253D&amp;md5=da053fa748721b6b381051a20e7a7f53</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref61" class="rightTabRefNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit61"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceresoli, D.</span></span> Pseudopotentials, <a href="https://sites.google.com/site/dceresoli/pseudopotentials" class="extLink">https://sites.google.com/site/dceresoli/pseudopotentials</a>.</span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        <script nonce="90f6f0279cee775c-LHR">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

        <span class="system-message-date">Sunday, February 09, 2025</span>
        <p>Please be aware that pubs.acs.org is undergoing maintenance from Saturday February 1 to Monday Febraury 3, that may have an impact on your experience. <script nonce="90f6f0279cee775c-LHR">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6f0279cee775c-LHR">
"use strict"

	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;

u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6f0279cee775c-LHR">
var currentJournal = "Journal of the American Chemical Society";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});
